The Manchu Qing emperors, especially Confucian scholar <a href="/wiki/Kangxi_Emperor" title="Kangxi Emperor">Kangxi</a>, remained largely conservative—retaining the bureaucracy and the scholars within it, as well as the Confucian ideals present in Chinese society. However, changes in the economy and new attempts at resolving certain issues occurred too. These included increased trade with Western countries that brought large amounts of silver into the Chinese economy in exchange for tea, <a href="/wiki/Porcelain" title="Porcelain">porcelain</a>, and silk textiles. This allowed for a new merchant-class, the <a href="/wiki/Comprador" title="Comprador">compradors</a>, to develop. In addition, repairs were done on existing <a href="/wiki/Levee" title="Levee">dikes</a>, canals, roadways, and <a href="/wiki/Irrigation" title="Irrigation">irrigation</a> works. This, combined with the lowering of taxes and government-assigned labor, was supposed to calm peasant unrest. However, the Qing failed to control the growing landlord class which had begun to exploit the peasantry and abuse their position.
</p><p>By the late 18th century, both internal and external issues began to arise in Qing China's politics, society, and economy. The exam system with which scholars were assigned into the bureaucracy became increasingly corrupt; bribes and other forms of cheating allowed for inexperienced and inept scholars to enter the bureaucracy and this eventually caused rampant neglect of the peasantry, military, and the previously mentioned infrastructure projects. Poverty and banditry steadily rose, especially in rural areas, and mass migrations looking for work throughout China occurred. The perpetually conservative government refused to make reforms that could resolve these issues.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Opium_War">Opium War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Opium War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/First_Opium_War" title="First Opium War">First Opium War</a></div>
<p>China saw its status reduced by what it perceived as parasitic trade with Westerners. Originally, European traders were at a disadvantage because the Chinese cared little for their goods, while European demand for Chinese commodities such as tea and porcelain only grew. In order to tip the trade imbalance in their favor, British merchants began to sell Indian <a href="/wiki/Opium" title="Opium">opium</a> to the Chinese. Not only did this sap Chinese bullion reserves, it also led to widespread drug addiction amongst the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scholar_official" title="Scholar official">bureaucracy</a> and society in general. A ban was placed on opium as early as 1729 by the <a href="/wiki/Yongzheng_Emperor" title="Yongzheng Emperor">Yongzheng Emperor</a>, but little was done to enforce it. By the early 19th century, under the new <a href="/wiki/Daoguang_Emperor" title="Daoguang Emperor">Daoguang Emperor</a>, the government began serious efforts to eradicate opium from Chinese society. Leading this endeavour were respected scholar-officials including <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Commissioner_(China)" title="Imperial Commissioner (China)">Imperial Commissioner</a> <a href="/wiki/Lin_Zexu" title="Lin Zexu">Lin Zexu</a>.
</p><p>After Lin <a href="/wiki/Destruction_of_opium_at_Humen" title="Destruction of opium at Humen">destroyed more than 20,000 chests of opium</a> in the summer of 1839, Europeans demanded compensation for what they saw as unwarranted Chinese interference in their affairs. When it was not paid, the British declared war later the same year, starting what became known as the <a href="/wiki/First_Opium_War" title="First Opium War">First Opium War</a>. The outdated Chinese <a href="/wiki/Junk_(ship)" title="Junk (ship)">junks</a> were no match for the advanced British gunboats, and soon the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yangzi_River" title="Yangzi River">Yangzi River</a> region came under threat of British bombardment and invasion. The emperor had no choice but to sue for peace, resulting in the exile of Lin and the making of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Nanking" title="Treaty of Nanking">Treaty of Nanking</a>, which ceded the British control of <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> and opened up trade and diplomacy with other European countries, including Germany, France, and the USA.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Inner_Manchuria">Inner Manchuria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Inner Manchuria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Northeast_China" title="Northeast China">Northeast China</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Manchuria" title="History of Manchuria">History of Manchuria</a></div>
<p>Northeast China came under influence of Russia with the building of the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Eastern_Railway" title="Chinese Eastern Railway">Chinese Eastern Railway</a> through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harbin,_China" title="Harbin, China">Harbin</a> to <a href="/wiki/Vladivostok" title="Vladivostok">Vladivostok</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Empire of Japan</a> replaced Russian influence in the region as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Japanese_War" title="Russo-Japanese War">Russo-Japanese War</a> in 1904–1905, and Japan laid the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Manchurian_Railway" title="South Manchurian Railway">South Manchurian Railway</a> in 1906 to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/L%C3%BCshunkou" title="Lüshunkou">Port Arthur</a>.  During the <a href="/wiki/Warlord_Era" title="Warlord Era">Warlord Era</a> in China, <a href="/wiki/Zhang_Zuolin" title="Zhang Zuolin">Zhang Zuolin</a> established himself in Northeast China, but was murdered by the Japanese for being too independent.  The former Chinese  emperor, <a href="/wiki/Puyi" title="Puyi">Puyi</a>, was then placed on the throne to lead a Japanese puppet state of <a href="/wiki/Manchukuo" title="Manchukuo">Manchukuo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup>  In August 1945, the Soviet Union invaded the region.  From 1945 to 1948, Northeast China was a base area for Mao Zedong's  <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army" title="People's Liberation Army">People's Liberation Army</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">Chinese Civil War</a>.  With the encouragement of the Kremlin, the area was used as a staging ground during the Civil War for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_China" title="Communist Party of China">Chinese Communists</a>, who were victorious in 1949 and have controlled ever since.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Joseon">Joseon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Joseon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Korea-Portrait_of_Emperor_Gojong-01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5886" data-file-width="3611" decoding="async" height="359" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Korea-Portrait_of_Emperor_Gojong-01.jpg/220px-Korea-Portrait_of_Emperor_Gojong-01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Korea-Portrait_of_Emperor_Gojong-01.jpg/330px-Korea-Portrait_of_Emperor_Gojong-01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Korea-Portrait_of_Emperor_Gojong-01.jpg/440px-Korea-Portrait_of_Emperor_Gojong-01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Korea-Portrait_of_Emperor_Gojong-01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Gojong_of_Korea" title="Gojong of Korea">Gojong</a> (1852–1919), the 26th king of <a href="/wiki/Joseon" title="Joseon">Joseon</a> dynasty and the first emperor of <a href="/wiki/Korean_Empire" title="Korean Empire">Korean Empire</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Deoksugung_Palace.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Deoksugung_Palace.jpg/220px-Deoksugung_Palace.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Deoksugung_Palace.jpg/330px-Deoksugung_Palace.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Deoksugung_Palace.jpg/440px-Deoksugung_Palace.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Deoksugung_Palace.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Deoksugung" title="Deoksugung">Deoksugung</a>, the palace where Emperor Gojong established <a href="/wiki/Korean_Empire" title="Korean Empire">Korean Empire</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>When it became the 19th century, the king of <a href="/wiki/Joseon" title="Joseon">Joseon</a> was powerless. Because the noble family of the king's wife got the power and ruled the country by their way. The 26th king of Joseon dynasty, <a href="/wiki/Gojong_of_Korea" title="Gojong of Korea">Gojong</a>'s father, <a href="/wiki/Heungseon_Daewongun" title="Heungseon Daewongun">Heungseon Daewongun</a> wanted the king be powerful again. Even he wasn't the king. As the father of young king, he destroyed noble families and corrupt organizations. So the royal family got the power again. But he wanted to rebuild <a href="/wiki/Gyeongbokgung" title="Gyeongbokgung">Gyeongbokgung</a> palace in order to show the royal power to people. So he was criticized by people because he spent enormous money and <a href="/wiki/Inflation" title="Inflation">inflation</a> occurred because of that. So his son, the real king <a href="/wiki/Gojong_of_Korea" title="Gojong of Korea">Gojong</a> got power.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Korean_Empire">Korean Empire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Korean Empire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The 26th king of <a href="/wiki/Joseon" title="Joseon">Joseon</a>, Gojong changed the nation's name to <i>Daehan Jeguk</i>. It means the <a href="/wiki/Korean_Empire" title="Korean Empire">Korean Empire</a>. And he also promoted himself as an emperor. The new empire accepted more western technology and strengthened military power. And <a href="/wiki/Korean_Empire" title="Korean Empire">Korean Empire</a> was going to become a <a href="/wiki/Neutral_Nation" title="Neutral Nation">Neutral Nation</a>. Unfortunately, in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russo-Japanese_war" title="Russo-Japanese war">Russo-Japanese war</a>, Japan ignored this, and eventually Japan won against <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>, and started to invade Korea. Japan first stole the right of diplomacy from Korean Empire illegally. But every western country ignored this invasion because they knew Japan became a strong country as they defeated Russian Empire. So emperor Gojong sent diplomats to a Dutch city known as <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a> to let everyone know that Japan stole the Empire's right illegally. But it was failed. Because the diplomats couldn't go into the conference room. Japan kicked Gojong off on the grounds that this reason. 3 years after, In 1910, Korean Empire became a part of Empire of Japan. It was the first time ever after invasion of Han dynasty in 108 BC.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary">Contemporary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Contemporary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_history" title="Contemporary history">Contemporary history</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:382px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Asia_(late_19th_century-_early_20th_century).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1387" data-file-width="1857" decoding="async" height="284" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Asia_%28late_19th_century-_early_20th_century%29.jpg/380px-Asia_%28late_19th_century-_early_20th_century%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Asia_%28late_19th_century-_early_20th_century%29.jpg/570px-Asia_%28late_19th_century-_early_20th_century%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Asia_%28late_19th_century-_early_20th_century%29.jpg/760px-Asia_%28late_19th_century-_early_20th_century%29.jpg 2x" width="380"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Asia_(late_19th_century-_early_20th_century).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Asia for early 20th century</div></div></div>
<p>The European powers had control of other parts of Asia by the early 20th century, such as <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">British India</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_Indochina" title="French Indochina">French Indochina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_East_Indies" title="Spanish East Indies">Spanish East Indies</a>, and Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a> and <a href="/wiki/Goa" title="Goa">Goa</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Great_Game" title="Great Game">Great Game</a> between Russia and Britain was the struggle for power in the Central Asian region in the nineteenth century. The <a href="/wiki/Trans-Siberian_Railway" title="Trans-Siberian Railway">Trans-Siberian Railway</a>, crossing Asia by train, was complete by 1916. Parts of Asia remained free from European control, although not influence, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persia" title="Persia">Persia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> and most of China. In the twentieth century, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imperial_Japan" title="Imperial Japan">Imperial Japan</a> expanded into China and Southeast Asia during the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. After the war, many Asian countries became independent from European powers. During the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, the northern parts of Asia were communist controlled with the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> and People's Republic of China, while western allies formed pacts such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CENTO" title="CENTO">CENTO</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SEATO" title="SEATO">SEATO</a>. Conflicts such as the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Afghan_War" title="Soviet–Afghan War">Soviet invasion of Afghanistan</a> were fought between communists and anti-communists. In the decades after the Second World War, a massive restructuring plan drove Japan to become the world's second-largest economy, a phenomenon known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_post-war_economic_miracle" title="Japanese post-war economic miracle">Japanese post-war economic miracle</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_conflict" title="Arab–Israeli conflict">Arab–Israeli conflict</a> has dominated much of the recent history of the Middle East. After the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>'s collapse in 1991, there were many new independent nations in Central Asia.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="China_2">China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Republic_of_China" title="History of the Republic of China">History of the Republic of China</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="History of the People's Republic of China">History of the People's Republic of China</a></div>
<p>Prior to <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, China faced a civil war between <a href="/wiki/Mao_Zedong" title="Mao Zedong">Mao Zedong</a>'s Communist party and <a href="/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek" title="Chiang Kai-shek">Chiang Kai-shek</a>'s nationalist party; the nationalists appeared to be in the lead. However, once the <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">Japanese invaded</a> in 1937, the two parties were forced to form a temporary cease-fire in order to defend China. The nationalists faced many military failures that caused them to lose territory and subsequently, respect from the Chinese masses. In contrast, the communists' use of guerilla warfare (led by <a href="/wiki/Lin_Biao" title="Lin Biao">Lin Biao</a>) proved effective against the Japanese's conventional methods and put the Communist Party on top by 1945. They also gained popularity for the reforms they were already applying in controlled areas, including land redistribution, education reforms, and widespread health care. For the next four years, the nationalists would be forced to retreat to the small island east of Fujian province, known as <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Taiwan" title="Geography of Taiwan">Taiwan</a> (formerly known as Formosa), where they remain today. In mainland China, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">People's Republic of China</a> was established by the Communist Party, with <a href="/wiki/Mao_Zedong" title="Mao Zedong">Mao Zedong</a> as its <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="President of the People's Republic of China">state chairman</a>.
</p><p>The communist government in China was defined by the party <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Professional_revolutionaries" title="Professional revolutionaries">cadres</a>. These hard-line officers controlled the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army" title="People's Liberation Army">People's Liberation Army</a>, which itself controlled large amounts of the bureaucracy. This system was further controlled by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Committee_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="Central Committee of the Communist Party of China">Central Committee</a>, which additionally supported the state chairman who was considered the head of the government. The People's Republic's foreign policies included the repressing of <a href="/wiki/Secession" title="Secession">secession</a> attempts in Mongolia and Tibet and supporting of <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Vietnam" title="North Vietnam">North Vietnam</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a>, respectively. By 1960 China and the USSR became adversaries, battling worldwide for control of local communist movements.
</p><p>Today China plays important roles in world economics and politics. China today is the world's second largest economy and the second fastest growing economy.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Indian_Subcontinent">Indian Subcontinent</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Indian Subcontinent">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From the mid-18th century to the mid-19th century, large regions of India were gradually annexed by the <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">East India Company</a>, a chartered company acting as a sovereign power on behalf of the British government. Dissatisfaction with <a href="/wiki/Company_rule_in_India" title="Company rule in India">company rule in India</a> led to the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Rebellion_of_1857" title="Indian Rebellion of 1857">Indian Rebellion of 1857</a>, which rocked parts of north and central India, and led to the dissolution of the company. India was afterwards ruled directly by the <a href="/wiki/The_Crown" title="The Crown">British Crown</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">British Raj</a>. After <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, a nationwide struggle for independence was launched by the <a href="/wiki/Indian_National_Congress" title="Indian National Congress">Indian National Congress</a>, led by <a href="/wiki/Mahatma_Gandhi" title="Mahatma Gandhi">Mahatma Gandhi</a>, and noted for <a href="/wiki/Nonviolent_resistance" title="Nonviolent resistance">nonviolence</a>. Later, the <a href="/wiki/All-India_Muslim_League" title="All-India Muslim League">All-India Muslim League</a> would advocate for a separate Muslim-majority <a href="/wiki/Nation_state" title="Nation state">nation state</a>. 
</p><p>In August 1947, the British Indian Empire was <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_India" title="Partition of India">partitioned</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_India" title="Dominion of India">Union of India</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Pakistan" title="Dominion of Pakistan">Dominion of Pakistan</a>. In particular, the partition of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Punjab_(British_India)" title="Punjab (British India)">Punjab</a> and Bengal led to rioting between Hindus, Muslims, and Sikhs in these provinces and spread to other nearby regions, leaving some 500,000 dead. The police and army units were largely ineffective. The British officers were gone, and the units were beginning to tolerate if not actually indulge in violence against their religious enemies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-symonds_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-symonds-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abid2014_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Abid2014-42">[42]</a></sup> Also, this period saw one of the largest mass migrations anywhere in modern history, with a total of 12 million Hindus, Sikhs and Muslims moving between the newly created nations of India and Pakistan (which gained independence on 15 and 14 August 1947 respectively).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-symonds_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-symonds-41">[41]</a></sup> In 1971, <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>, formerly <a href="/wiki/East_Pakistan" title="East Pakistan">East Pakistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Bengal" title="East Bengal">East Bengal</a>, seceded from Pakistan<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Raghavan2013_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Raghavan2013-43">[43]</a></sup> through an <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Liberation_War" title="Bangladesh Liberation War">armed conflict</a> sparked by the rise of the <a href="/wiki/Bengali_nationalism" title="Bengali nationalism">Bengali nationalist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Self-determination" title="Self-determination">self-determination</a> movement.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Korea_2">Korea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Korea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2018_inter-Korean_summit_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="943" data-file-width="1415" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/2018_inter-Korean_summit_01.jpg/220px-2018_inter-Korean_summit_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/2018_inter-Korean_summit_01.jpg/330px-2018_inter-Korean_summit_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/2018_inter-Korean_summit_01.jpg/440px-2018_inter-Korean_summit_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2018_inter-Korean_summit_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The third Inter-Korean Summit, which was  held in 2018, between South Korean president <a href="/wiki/Moon_Jae-in" title="Moon Jae-in">Moon Jae-in</a> and North Korean supreme leader <a href="/wiki/Kim_Jong-un" title="Kim Jong-un">Kim Jong-un</a>. It was a historical event that symbolized the peace of Asia.</div></div></div>
<p>During the period when the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a> occurred, Korea divided into North and South. <a href="/wiki/Syngman_Rhee" title="Syngman Rhee">Syngman Rhee</a> became the first president of <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kim_Il-sung" title="Kim Il-sung">Kim Il-sung</a> became the supreme leader of <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a>. After the war, the president of South Korea, Syngman Rhee tries to become a dictator. So the <a href="/wiki/April_Revolution" title="April Revolution">April Revolution</a> occurred, eventually <a href="/wiki/Syngman_Rhee" title="Syngman Rhee">Syngman Rhee</a> was exiled from his country. 
In 1963, <a href="/wiki/Park_Chung-hee" title="Park Chung-hee">Park Chung-hee</a> was empowered with a  military coup d'état. He dispatched <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Korea_Army" title="Republic of Korea Army">Republic of Korea Army</a> to <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a>. And during this age, the economy of <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a> outran that of <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a>.
</p><p>Although <a href="/wiki/Park_Chung-hee" title="Park Chung-hee">Park Chung-hee</a> improved the nation's economy, he was a dictator, so people didn't like him. Eventually, he is murdered by <a href="/wiki/Kim_Jae-gyu" title="Kim Jae-gyu">Kim Jae-gyu</a>. In 1979, <a href="/wiki/Chun_Doo-hwan" title="Chun Doo-hwan">Chun Doo-hwan</a> was empowered by another coup d’état by military. He oppressed the resistances in the city of <a href="/wiki/Gwangju" title="Gwangju">Gwangju</a>. That event is called 'Gwangju Uprising'. Despite the Gwangju Uprising, <a href="/wiki/Chun_Doo-hwan" title="Chun Doo-hwan">Chun Doo-hwan</a> became the president. But the people resisted again in 1987. This movement is called '<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/June_Struggle" title="June Struggle">June Struggle</a>'. As a result of <a href="/wiki/Gwangju_Uprising" title="Gwangju Uprising">Gwangju Uprising</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/June_Struggle" title="June Struggle">June Struggle</a>, South Korea finally became a democratic republic in 1987.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Roh_Tae-woo" title="Roh Tae-woo">Roh Tae-woo</a> (1988–93),  <a href="/wiki/Kim_Young-sam" title="Kim Young-sam">Kim Young-sam</a> (1993–98), <a href="/wiki/Kim_Dae-jung" title="Kim Dae-jung">Kim Dae-jung</a> (1998–2003), <a href="/wiki/Roh_Moo-hyun" title="Roh Moo-hyun">Roh Moo-hyun</a> (2003–2008), <a href="/wiki/Lee_Myung-bak" title="Lee Myung-bak">Lee Myung-bak</a> (2008–2013), <a href="/wiki/Park_Geun-hye" title="Park Geun-hye">Park Geun-hye</a> (2013–2017), <a href="/wiki/Moon_Jae-in" title="Moon Jae-in">Moon Jae-in</a> (2017–) were elected as a president in order after 1987.  In 1960, <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> was far wealthier than <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>. But in 1970, South Korea begins to outrun the North Korean economy. In 2018, South Korea is ranked #10 in world <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GDP" title="GDP">GDP</a> ranking.
</p>

The murderous mobs were well supplied with arms, such as daggers, swords, spears and fire-arms. (A former civil servant mentioned in his autobiography that weapon supplies had been sent from NWFP and money was supplied by Delhi-based politicians.)</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Nation&amp;rft.atitle=The+forgotten+massacre&amp;rft.date=2014-12-29&amp;rft.aulast=Abid&amp;rft.aufirst=Abdul+Majeed&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fnation.com.pk%2F29-Dec-2014%2Fthe-forgotten-massacre&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHistory+of+Asia"></span></span>
